Conditions for Takfir Against Deniers of Mutawatir Matters
Ghazali outlines conditions for takfir against deniers of mutawatir matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conditions under which denying a mutawatir report leads to takfir, including the exception for recent converts and the distinction between essential and non-essential matters.

Core Idea
Not every denial of a mutawatir report makes one a disbeliever.

Ghazali begins by clarifying a crucial point: while denying matters known by mass transmission (tawatur) generally incurs takfir, there are important nuances. He explains that such matters are grasped by both commoners and elites, but the ruling depends on whether the person has received the tawatur and whether the matter is a fundamental of religion. This lesson unpacks those conditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Ghazali states the general rule and then immediately provides exceptions.
The passage is concise; pay attention to the shift from general to specific.
2
Identify the conditions for takfir
Look for the condition that the person must have received the tawatur (not a recent convert) and that the denied matter must be a fundamental of religion (like Hajj, prayer, pillars of Islam).
Ghazali gives examples of non-fundamentals: specific battles, the Prophet's marriage to Hafsa, existence of Abu Bakr.
3
Ask: Why does Ghazali exempt recent converts?
Consider that knowledge through tawatur requires exposure to widespread reports. A new Muslim may not have encountered them yet. This shows Ghazali's concern for fairness.
This connects to the broader principle of excusing ignorance in matters of detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا أيضاً ينبغي أن يُحْكم بكفرِهِ ؛ لأنَّه مكذِّبٌ ولكنه محترز عن حقيقة التكذيب، ولكنهم التصريح، وإلا فالمتواتراتُ يشترك في دركها العوام والخواص، وليس يخشون التصريح بطلان ما يقولُه كبطلان مذهب المعتزلة؛ فإنَّ ذلك يختص بدركِهِ أولو البصائر من النظار، إلا أن يكون هذا الشخص قريب العهد بالإسلام ولم تتواتر عندَه بعد هذه الأمورُ، فنمهله إلى أن تتواتر عنده، ولسنا نكفره لأنه أنكر أمراً معلوماً بالتواتر؛ فإنه لو أنكر غزوةً من غزواتِ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المتواترة أو أنكر نكاحه حفصة بنت عمر رضي الله عنه، أو أنكر وجودَ أبي بكر رضي الله عنه وخلافته لم يلزم تكفيره؛ لأنه ليس تكذيباً في أصل من أصول الدين مما يجب التصديقُ به، بخلاف الحج والصلاة وأركان الإسلام. ولسنا نكفّره بمخالفته الإجماع؛ فإنَّ لنا نظراً في تكفير النظام المنكرِ لأصل الإجماع؛ لأن الشبهة كثيرة في كون الإجماع حجة قاطعة، وإنما الإجماع عبارة عن التطابق على رأي نظري، وهذا الذي نحن فيه تطابق على الإخبار عن محسوس، وتطابق العدد الكثير على الإخبار عن محسوس على سبيل التواتر يوجب العلم الضروري، وتطابق أهل الحل والعقد على رأي واحد نظري لا يوجب العلم إلا من جهة الشرع، ولذلك لا يجوز أن يستدل على حدث العالم بتواتر الأخبار من النظار الذين حكموا به، بل لا تواتر إلا في المحسوسات. الرتبة السادسة: ألا يصرح بالتكذيب ولا يكذِّبَ أيضاً أمراً معلوماً بأصل القطع بالتواتر من أصول الدين، ولكن ينكر ما علم صحته بالإجماع المجرَّدِ، فلا مدرك لصحته إلا الإجماع، فأما التواتر فلا يشهد له؛ كالنظام مثلاً إذ أنكر كون الإجماع حجَّةً قاطعة في أصله، وقال: ليس يدلُّ على استحالة الخطا على أهل الإجماع دليل عقلي قاطع ولا شرعي متواتر لا يحتمل التأويل، فكلُّ ما يُستشهَدُ به من الأخبار والآيات مؤوّل بزعمه، وهو في قوله هذا خارق لإجماع التابعين، فإنّا نعلم إجماعهم على أن ما أجمع عليه الصحابة حق مقطوع به لا يمكن خلافه، فقد أنكر الإجماع وخرق الإجماع. وهذا في محلّ الاجتهاد، ولي فيه نظر؛ إذ الإشكالات كثيرة في وجه كون الإجماع حجَّةً، فيكاد يكون ذلك كالممهد للعذر، ولكن لو فُتِحَ هذا الباب انجرَّ إلى أمور شنيعة، وهو أن قائلاً لو قال: يجوز أن يُبعث رسول بعد نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فيبعد التوقفُ في تكفيره ومستند استحالة ذلك عند البحث يُستمَدُّ من الإجماع لا محالة؛ فإنَّ العقل لا يحيلُه، وما نقل فيه من قوله: «لا نبي بعدي»، ومن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّنَ﴾ فلا يعجز هذا القائل عن تأويله فيقول: «خاتم النبيين» أراد به أولي العزم من الرسل؛ فإن قوله: «النبيين» عام ولا يبعد تخصيص العام، وقوله: «لا نبي بعدي» لم يرد به الرسول، وفرق بين النبي والرسول، والنبيُّ أعلى رتبةٌ من الرسول إلى غير ذلك من أنواع الهذيان. فهذا وأمثالُهُ لا يمكنُ أن تُدْعَى استحالته من حيث مجرد اللفظ؛ فإنا في تأويل ظواهر التشبيه قضينا باحتمالاتٍ أبعد من هذه ولم يكن ذلك مبطلاً للنصوص، ولكن الردَّ على هذا القائل أنَّ الأمة فهمت بالإجماع من هذا ومن قرائن أحواله أنه أفهم عدم نبي بعده أبداً وعدم رسول أبداً، وأنه ليس فيه تأويل ولا تخصيص، فمنكر هذا لا يكون إلا منكراً للإجماع، وعند هذا يتفرع مسائل متقاربة مشتبكة يفتقر كلُّ واحدة منها إلى نظرٍ.
This also should be judged as his disbelief; because he is a denier, but he is cautious about the reality of denial, but they are explicit. Otherwise, matters known by mutawatir (mass transmission) are grasped by commoners and elites alike, and they do not fear to explicitly state the falsehood of what he says, like the falsehood of the Mu'tazilite school; for that is grasped only by those of insight among the investigators. Unless this person is a recent convert to Islam and these matters have not yet become mutawatir for him, then we give him time until they become mutawatir for him. And we do not declare him a disbeliever because he denied a matter known by tawatur; for if he denied a battle from the mutawatir battles of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, or denied his marriage to Hafsa bint Umar, may God be pleased with them, or denied the existence of Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, and his caliphate, his takfir would not be necessary; because it is not a denial of a fundamental of religion that must be believed, unlike the Hajj, prayer, and the pillars of Islam. And we do not declare him a disbeliever for contradicting consensus (ijma); for we have a consideration in declaring an-Nazzam a disbeliever for denying the principle of consensus; because the doubt is great concerning consensus being a decisive proof. Consensus is merely an agreement on a theoretical opinion. What we are dealing with here is agreement on reporting something perceptible, and the agreement of a large number on reporting something perceptible by way of tawatur produces necessary knowledge. But the agreement of the people of binding and loosing on a single theoretical opinion does not produce knowledge except from the side of the Law. Therefore, it is not permissible to use the tawatur of reports from the investigators who ruled on it to prove the temporal origination of the world; rather, there is no tawatur except in perceptibles. The sixth rank: That he does not explicitly deny, nor does he deny a matter known by definitive tawatur from the fundamentals of religion, but he denies something whose correctness is known by mere consensus (ijma mujarrad), so there is no basis for its correctness except consensus. As for tawatur, it does not attest to it. For example, an-Nazzam, when he denied that consensus is a decisive proof in principle, and said: There is no rational decisive proof nor a mutawatir legal proof that cannot be interpreted to indicate the impossibility of error upon the people of consensus. So all the reports and verses that are cited are interpreted according to his claim. In this statement of his, he violates the consensus of the Successors (tabi'un), for we know their consensus that what the Companions agreed upon is a definite truth, whose opposition is impossible. So he denied consensus and violated consensus. This is in a matter of ijtihad, and I have difficulty with it; for the problems are many concerning the fact that consensus is a proof. That almost becomes a preparation for an excuse. But if this door were opened, it would lead to abominable matters. That is, if someone said: It is permissible that a messenger be sent after our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, then hesitation in declaring him a disbeliever would be far-fetched. The basis for the impossibility of that, upon investigation, is necessarily derived from consensus; for reason does not deem it impossible. And what is transmitted about it from his saying, 'There is no prophet after me,' and from His saying, 'and the seal of the prophets,' this speaker would not be unable to interpret it. He would say: 'The seal of the prophets' means the prophets of determination (ulu al-azm). For His saying 'the prophets' is general, and it is not unlikely to specify a general. And his saying 'There is no prophet after me' does not refer to a messenger, and there is a difference between a prophet and a messenger, and the prophet is of a higher rank than the messenger... and other types of delirium. This and its likes cannot be claimed to be impossible from the mere wording; for we, in interpreting the apparent meanings of anthropomorphism, have judged by possibilities more remote than these, and that did not nullify the texts. But the refutation of this speaker is that the ummah understood by consensus, from this and from circumstantial evidence of his states, that he made understood that there is no prophet after him ever, and no messenger ever, and that there is no interpretation nor specification in it. So the denier of this is only a denier of consensus. And at this point, many interrelated and tangled issues branch off, each of which requires investigation.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a classification of different levels of denial and their implications for takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever). Imam Ghazali begins by reasserting that a person who denies matters known by tawatur (mass transmission) should be judged a disbeliever, but with a caveat: such matters are grasped by both commoners and elites. However, if the person is a recent convert and the tawatur has not yet reached him, we give him time. Denying something like a specific battle or the marriage of the Prophet does not entail takfir because it is not a fundamental of religion. But denying the Hajj, prayer, or the pillars of Islam does. Then Ghazali turns to consensus (ijma). He says we do not declare a person a disbeliever merely for rejecting consensus because there is a great deal of doubt about whether consensus provides decisive certainty. He distinguishes between tawatur (which produces necessary knowledge) and ijma (which is a theoretical agreement). The sixth rank is when a person does not deny something known by tawatur but denies something known only by mere consensus (ijma mujarrad), such as an-Nazzam denying that consensus is a decisive proof. Ghazali notes that an-Nazzam violated the consensus of the Successors. Ghazali then says this is a matter of ijtihad and he has difficulty with it because there are many problems with consensus being a proof. However, if we open the door to rejecting consensus, it could lead to abominable claims like the possibility of a prophet after Muhammad. Reason alone does not prohibit it; only consensus does. And the denier would interpret the texts. Ghazali argues that the ummah understood by consensus that there is no prophet after Muhammad, and this understanding is based on the Prophet's words and circumstantial evidence. So the denier is essentially a denier of consensus. The passage ends by noting that this issue branches into many interconnected matters.

Key Terms
تواتر
تكفير
أركان الإسلام
علم ضروري

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why does denying a mutawatir battle of the Prophet not necessarily lead to takfir?
A) Because battles are not reported by tawatur.
B) Because it is not a fundamental of religion.
C) Because the person may be a recent convert.
D) Because takfir only applies to denying the existence of prophets.

Key Takeaway
Denying a mutawatir report leads to takfir only if the report is a fundamental of religion and the person has received the tawatur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a well-known truth of Islam simply because it was inconvenient to your lifestyle? What would it mean for you to submit fully, not just to the easy teachings but to every mutawatir command?
?
Imagine you are the recent convert Ghazali mentions—someone who has not yet internalized a fundamental belief. Do you have the humility to wait until the truth becomes undeniable for you, or do you rush to accept or reject based on incomplete knowledge?
?
When you hear about a matter of religion that is widely accepted by scholars but personally unclear to you, do you trust the consensus of the community or do you feel entitled to deny it until you yourself are convinced? How does your answer align with Ghazali's ruling?

Rational Judgments

The Distinction Between Tawatur and Ijma in Certainty
Ghazali distinguishes tawatur from ijma in terms of certainty and necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali distinguishes tawatur (which produces necessary knowledge) from ijma (which provides only theoretical certainty) and why this matters for takfir.

Core Idea
Tawatur yields necessary knowledge; ijma yields only theoretical certainty based on revelation.

After discussing the ruling on mutawatir matters, Ghazali turns to the role of consensus (ijma). He argues that contradicting ijma does not automatically incur takfir because ijma is not a source of necessary knowledge. He contrasts the agreement of a large number on a perceived object (tawatur) with the agreement of scholars on a theoretical opinion (ijma). This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on tawatur vs ijma
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note how Ghazali defines each and their epistemic value.
The key sentence: 'تطابق العدد الكثير على الإخبار عن محسوس على سبيل التواتر يوجب العلم الضروري' vs 'تطابق أهل الحل والعقد على رأي واحد نظري لا يوجب العلم إلا من جهة الشرع.'
2
Identify the epistemological difference
Tawatur about perceptibles gives necessary knowledge (direct certainty). Ijma on a theoretical matter gives knowledge only through revelation (i.e., it is a legal proof, not rational).
This explains why Ghazali does not immediately declare a person a disbeliever for rejecting ijma.
3
Ask: Why does Ghazali mention the example of the world's temporal origination?
He says tawatur of reports from investigators about the world's origination does not produce necessary knowledge because it is not about a perceptible matter. This reinforces that tawatur only applies to sensory objects.
This is a critique of using tawatur in theological arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا أيضاً ينبغي أن يُحْكم بكفرِهِ ؛ لأنَّه مكذِّبٌ ولكنه محترز عن حقيقة التكذيب، ولكنهم التصريح، وإلا فالمتواتراتُ يشترك في دركها العوام والخواص، وليس يخشون التصريح بطلان ما يقولُه كبطلان مذهب المعتزلة؛ فإنَّ ذلك يختص بدركِهِ أولو البصائر من النظار، إلا أن يكون هذا الشخص قريب العهد بالإسلام ولم تتواتر عندَه بعد هذه الأمورُ، فنمهله إلى أن تتواتر عنده، ولسنا نكفره لأنه أنكر أمراً معلوماً بالتواتر؛ فإنه لو أنكر غزوةً من غزواتِ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المتواترة أو أنكر نكاحه حفصة بنت عمر رضي الله عنه، أو أنكر وجودَ أبي بكر رضي الله عنه وخلافته لم يلزم تكفيره؛ لأنه ليس تكذيباً في أصل من أصول الدين مما يجب التصديقُ به، بخلاف الحج والصلاة وأركان الإسلام. ولسنا نكفّره بمخالفته الإجماع؛ فإنَّ لنا نظراً في تكفير النظام المنكرِ لأصل الإجماع؛ لأن الشبهة كثيرة في كون الإجماع حجة قاطعة، وإنما الإجماع عبارة عن التطابق على رأي نظري، وهذا الذي نحن فيه تطابق على الإخبار عن محسوس، وتطابق العدد الكثير على الإخبار عن محسوس على سبيل التواتر يوجب العلم الضروري، وتطابق أهل الحل والعقد على رأي واحد نظري لا يوجب العلم إلا من جهة الشرع، ولذلك لا يجوز أن يستدل على حدث العالم بتواتر الأخبار من النظار الذين حكموا به، بل لا تواتر إلا في المحسوسات. الرتبة السادسة: ألا يصرح بالتكذيب ولا يكذِّبَ أيضاً أمراً معلوماً بأصل القطع بالتواتر من أصول الدين، ولكن ينكر ما علم صحته بالإجماع المجرَّدِ، فلا مدرك لصحته إلا الإجماع، فأما التواتر فلا يشهد له؛ كالنظام مثلاً إذ أنكر كون الإجماع حجَّةً قاطعة في أصله، وقال: ليس يدلُّ على استحالة الخطا على أهل الإجماع دليل عقلي قاطع ولا شرعي متواتر لا يحتمل التأويل، فكلُّ ما يُستشهَدُ به من الأخبار والآيات مؤوّل بزعمه، وهو في قوله هذا خارق لإجماع فيكاد يكون ذلك كالممهد للعذر، ولكن لو فُتِحَ هذا الباب انجرَّ إلى أمور شنيعة، وهو أن قائلاً لو قال: يجوز أن يُبعث رسول بعد نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فيبعد التوقفُ في تكفيره ومستند استحالة ذلك عند البحث يُستمَدُّ من الإجماع لا محالة؛ فإنَّ العقل لا يحيلُه، وما نقل فيه من قوله: «لا نبي بعدي»، ومن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّنَ﴾ فلا يعجز هذا القائل عن تأويله فيقول: «خاتم النبيين» أراد به أولي العزم من الرسل؛ فإن قوله: «النبيين» عام ولا يبعد تخصيص العام، وقوله: «لا نبي بعدي» لم يرد به الرسول، وفرق بين النبي والرسول، والنبيُّ أعلى رتبةٌ من الرسول إلى غير ذلك من أنواع الهذيان. فهذا وأمثالُهُ لا يمكنُ أن تُدْعَى استحالته من حيث مجرد اللفظ؛ فإنا في تأويل ظواهر التشبيه قضينا باحتمالاتٍ أبعد من هذه ولم يكن ذلك مبطلاً للنصوص، ولكن الردَّ على هذا القائل أنَّ الأمة فهمت بالإجماع من هذا ومن قرائن أحواله أنه أفهم عدم نبي بعده أبداً وعدم رسول أبداً، وأنه ليس فيه تأويل ولا تخصيص، فمنكر هذا لا يكون إلا منكراً للإجماع، وعند هذا يتفرع مسائل متقاربة مشتبكة يفتقر كلُّ واحدة منها إلى نظرٍ.
This also should be judged as his disbelief; because he is a denier, but he is cautious about the reality of denial, but they are explicit. Otherwise, matters known by mutawatir (mass transmission) are grasped by commoners and elites alike, and they do not fear to explicitly state the falsehood of what he says, like the falsehood of the Mu'tazilite school; for that is grasped only by those of insight among the investigators. Unless this person is a recent convert to Islam and these matters have not yet become mutawatir for him, then we give him time until they become mutawatir for him. And we do not declare him a disbeliever because he denied a matter known by tawatur; for if he denied a battle from the mutawatir battles of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, or denied his marriage to Hafsa bint Umar, may God be pleased with them, or denied the existence of Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, and his caliphate, his takfir would not be necessary; because it is not a denial of a fundamental of religion that must be believed, unlike the Hajj, prayer, and the pillars of Islam. And we do not declare him a disbeliever for contradicting consensus (ijma); for we have a consideration in declaring an-Nazzam a disbeliever for denying the principle of consensus; because the doubt is great concerning consensus being a decisive proof. Consensus is merely an agreement on a theoretical opinion. What we are dealing with here is agreement on reporting something perceptible, and the agreement of a large number on reporting something perceptible by way of tawatur produces necessary knowledge. But the agreement of the people of binding and loosing on a single theoretical opinion does not produce knowledge except from the side of the Law. Therefore, it is not permissible to use the tawatur of reports from the investigators who ruled on it to prove the temporal origination of the world; rather, there is no tawatur except in perceptibles. The sixth rank: That he does not explicitly deny, nor does he deny a matter known by definitive tawatur from the fundamentals of religion, but he denies something whose correctness is known by mere consensus (ijma mujarrad), so there is no basis for its correctness except consensus. As for tawatur, it does not attest to it. For example, an-Nazzam, when he denied that consensus is a decisive proof in principle, and said: There is no rational decisive proof nor a mutawatir legal proof that cannot be interpreted to indicate the impossibility of error upon the people of consensus. So all the reports and verses that are cited are interpreted according to his claim. In this statement of his, he violates the consensus of the Successors (tabi'un), for we know their consensus that what the Companions agreed upon is a definite truth, whose opposition is impossible. So he denied consensus and violated consensus. This is in a matter of ijtihad, and I have difficulty with it; for the problems are many concerning the fact that consensus is a proof. That almost becomes a preparation for an excuse. But if this door were opened, it would lead to abominable matters. That is, if someone said: It is permissible that a messenger be sent after our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, then hesitation in declaring him a disbeliever would be far-fetched. The basis for the impossibility of that, upon investigation, is necessarily derived from consensus; for reason does not deem it impossible. And what is transmitted about it from his saying, 'There is no prophet after me,' and from His saying, 'and the seal of the prophets,' this speaker would not be unable to interpret it. He would say: 'The seal of the prophets' means the prophets of determination (ulu al-azm). For His saying 'the prophets' is general, and it is not unlikely to specify a general. And his saying 'There is no prophet after me' does not refer to a messenger, and there is a difference between a prophet and a messenger, and the prophet is of a higher rank than the messenger... and other types of delirium. This and its likes cannot be claimed to be impossible from the mere wording; for we, in interpreting the apparent meanings of anthropomorphism, have judged by possibilities more remote than these, and that did not nullify the texts. But the refutation of this speaker is that the ummah understood by consensus, from this and from circumstantial evidence of his states, that he made understood that there is no prophet after him ever, and no messenger ever, and that there is no interpretation nor specification in it. So the denier of this is only a denier of consensus. And at this point, many interrelated and tangled issues branch off, each of which requires investigation.

Commentary
This passage is a classification of different levels of denial and their implications for takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever). Imam Ghazali begins by reasserting that a person who denies matters known by tawatur (mass transmission) should be judged a disbeliever, but with a caveat: such matters are grasped by both commoners and elites. However, if the person is a recent convert and the tawatur has not yet reached him, we give him time. Denying something like a specific battle or the marriage of the Prophet does not entail takfir because it is not a fundamental of religion. But denying the Hajj, prayer, or the pillars of Islam does. Then Ghazali turns to consensus (ijma). He says we do not declare a person a disbeliever merely for rejecting consensus because there is a great deal of doubt about whether consensus provides decisive certainty. He distinguishes between tawatur (which produces necessary knowledge) and ijma (which is a theoretical agreement). The sixth rank is when a person does not deny something known by tawatur but denies something known only by mere consensus (ijma mujarrad), such as an-Nazzam denying that consensus is a decisive proof. Ghazali notes that an-Nazzam violated the consensus of the Successors. Ghazali then says this is a matter of ijtihad and he has difficulty with it because there are many problems with consensus being a proof. However, if we open the door to rejecting consensus, it could lead to abominable claims like the possibility of a prophet after Muhammad. Reason alone does not prohibit it; only consensus does. And the denier would interpret the texts. Ghazali argues that the ummah understood by consensus that there is no prophet after Muhammad, and this understanding is based on the Prophet's words and circumstantial evidence. So the denier is essentially a denier of consensus. The passage ends by noting that this issue branches into many interconnected matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that ijma is as certain as tawatur and rejecting it always necessitates takfir.
Correction: Ghazali explains that ijma on theoretical matters does not produce necessary knowledge; it is a legal proof that is open to doubt.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what type of knowledge does tawatur about perceptibles produce?
A) Theoretical knowledge
B) Necessary knowledge
C) Probable knowledge
D) Legal knowledge

Key Takeaway
Tawatur about perceptibles gives necessary certainty; ijma about theoretical matters gives only revealed certainty, which is open to debate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of your beliefs about Islam do you hold with the certainty of tawatur, and which are actually based on theoretical opinions (like ijma)? How would it change your commitment if you realized some of your convictions are not necessarily certain?
?
When you trust reports about religious matters, do you subject them to the same scrutiny Ghazali applies—distinguishing perceptibles from theories? What would it take for you to admit that some of your theological positions might be merely probable, not certain?
?
Consider a disagreement you have with other Muslims. Is your confidence in your position based on tawatur (undeniable reports) or on theoretical reasoning? Would you be able to respect the other side if you saw their position as based on a different theoretical consensus? What would that require of your humility?

Rational Judgments

The Sixth Rank: Denial of Matters Known Only by Ijma
Ghazali defines the sixth rank of denial and explores the implications of basing takfir on consensus alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth rank of denial – where a person denies something known only by consensus (ijma mujarrad) – and Ghazali's analysis of its implications, including the dangerous consequences for core beliefs like the finality of prophethood.

Core Idea
Denying matters proven solely by consensus opens the door to extreme claims, but Ghazali hesitates to declare takfir on this basis alone.

Ghazali now introduces the sixth rank, which involves a person who does not deny anything known by tawatur but denies something whose only proof is consensus. He uses the example of an-Nazzam, who rejected the authority of ijma entirely. This leads Ghazali to reflect on the difficulties of using ijma as a decisive proof. He then warns that if we allow rejection of consensus, it could lead to absurdities like claiming a prophet after Muhammad, which would require refutation not from texts alone but from the consensus of the ummah. This lesson delves into that complex argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the sixth rank definition
Read the opening lines of the passage where Ghazali defines the sixth rank. Notice that it is about denying something known by mere consensus (ijma mujarrad), not tawatur.
The key phrase: 'ينكر ما علم صحته بالإجماع المجرد'.
2
Analyze the example of an-Nazzam
Ghazali uses an-Nazzam as an example: he denied that consensus is a decisive proof. Ghazali notes that an-Nazzam also violated the consensus of the Successors (tabi'un).
This shows the tension: rejecting the validity of ijma while simultaneously violating an actual consensus.
3
Understand Ghazali's hesitation
Ghazali says 'ولي فيه نظر' (I have difficulty with it), acknowledging that the issue of ijma's authority is open to scholarly debate.
He fears that opening the door to rejecting ijma could lead to harmful innovations.
4
Examine the dangerous consequence
Ghazali presents a hypothetical: if someone claims a prophet after Muhammad, the only proof against it is consensus. The denier could interpret texts to escape literal meaning. The refutation is that the ummah understood by consensus that no prophet comes after Muhammad.
This shows that in such cases, the only safeguard is the consensus of the ummah.

فهذا أيضاً ينبغي أن يُحْكم بكفرِهِ ؛ لأنَّه مكذِّبٌ ولكنه محترز عن حقيقة التكذيب، ولكنهم التصريح، وإلا فالمتواتراتُ يشترك في دركها العوام والخواص، وليس يخشون التصريح بطلان ما يقولُه كبطلان مذهب المعتزلة؛ فإنَّ ذلك يختص بدركِهِ أولو البصائر من النظار، إلا أن يكون هذا الشخص قريب العهد بالإسلام ولم تتواتر عندَه بعد هذه الأمورُ، فنمهله إلى أن تتواتر عنده، ولسنا نكفره لأنه أنكر أمراً معلوماً بالتواتر؛ فإنه لو أنكر غزوةً من غزواتِ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المتواترة أو أنكر نكاحه حفصة بنت عمر رضي الله عنه، أو أنكر وجودَ أبي بكر رضي الله عنه وخلافته لم يلزم تكفيره؛ لأنه ليس تكذيباً في أصل من أصول الدين مما يجب التصديقُ به، بخلاف الحج والصلاة وأركان الإسلام. ولسنا نكفّره بمخالفته الإجماع؛ فإنَّ لنا نظراً في تكفير النظام المنكرِ لأصل الإجماع؛ لأن الشبهة كثيرة في كون الإجماع حجة قاطعة، وإنما الإجماع عبارة عن التطابق على رأي نظري، وهذا الذي نحن فيه تطابق على الإخبار عن محسوس، وتطابق العدد الكثير على الإخبار عن محسوس على سبيل التواتر يوجب العلم الضروري، وتطابق أهل الحل والعقد على رأي واحد نظري لا يوجب العلم إلا من جهة الشرع، ولذلك لا يجوز أن يستدل على حدث العالم بتواتر الأخبار من النظار الذين حكموا به، بل لا تواتر إلا في المحسوسات. الرتبة السادسة: ألا يصرح بالتكذيب ولا يكذِّبَ أيضاً أمراً معلوماً بأصل القطع بالتواتر من أصول الدين، ولكن ينكر ما علم صحته بالإجماع المجرَّدِ، فلا مدرك لصحته إلا الإجماع، فأما التواتر فلا يشهد له؛ كالنظام مثلاً إذ أنكر كون الإجماع حجَّةً قاطعة في أصله، وقال: ليس يدلُّ على استحالة الخطا على أهل الإجماع دليل عقلي قاطع ولا شرعي متواتر لا يحتمل التأويل، فكلُّ ما يُستشهَدُ به من الأخبار والآيات مؤوّل بزعمه، وهو في قوله هذا خارق لإجماع التابعين، فإنّا نعلم إجماعهم على أن ما أجمع عليه الصحابة حق مقطوع به لا يمكن خلافه، فقد أنكر الإجماع وخرق الإجماع. وهذا في محلّ الاجتهاد، ولي فيه نظر؛ إذ الإشكالات كثيرة في وجه كون الإجماع حجَّةً، فيكاد يكون ذلك كالممهد للعذر، ولكن لو فُتِحَ هذا الباب انجرَّ إلى أمور شنيعة، وهو أن قائلاً لو قال: يجوز أن يُبعث رسول بعد نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فيبعد التوقفُ في تكفيره ومستند استحالة ذلك عند البحث يُستمَدُّ من الإجماع لا محالة؛ فإنَّ العقل لا يحيلُه، وما نقل فيه من قوله: «لا نبي بعدي»، ومن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّنَ﴾ فلا يعجز هذا القائل عن تأويله فيقول: «خاتم النبيين» أراد به أولي العزم من الرسل؛ فإن قوله: «النبيين» عام ولا يبعد تخصيص العام، وقوله: «لا نبي بعدي» لم يرد به الرسول، وفرق بين النبي والرسول، والنبيُّ أعلى رتبةٌ من الرسول إلى غير ذلك من أنواع الهذيان. فهذا وأمثالُهُ لا يمكنُ أن تُدْعَى استحالته من حيث مجرد اللفظ؛ فإنا في تأويل ظواهر التشبيه قضينا باحتمالاتٍ أبعد من هذه ولم يكن ذلك مبطلاً للنصوص، ولكن الردَّ على هذا القائل أنَّ الأمة فهمت بالإجماع من هذا ومن قرائن أحواله أنه أفهم عدم نبي بعده أبداً وعدم رسول أبداً، وأنه ليس فيه تأويل ولا تخصيص، فمنكر هذا لا يكون إلا منكراً للإجماع، وعند هذا يتفرع مسائل متقاربة مشتبكة يفتقر كلُّ واحدة منها إلى نظرٍ.
This also should be judged as his disbelief; because he is a denier, but he is cautious about the reality of denial, but they are explicit. Otherwise, matters known by mutawatir (mass transmission) are grasped by commoners and elites alike, and they do not fear to explicitly state the falsehood of what he says, like the falsehood of the Mu'tazilite school; for that is grasped only by those of insight among the investigators. Unless this person is a recent convert to Islam and these matters have not yet become mutawatir for him, then we give him time until they become mutawatir for him. And we do not declare him a disbeliever because he denied a matter known by tawatur; for if he denied a battle from the mutawatir battles of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, or denied his marriage to Hafsa bint Umar, may God be pleased with them, or denied the existence of Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, and his caliphate, his takfir would not be necessary; because it is not a denial of a fundamental of religion that must be believed, unlike the Hajj, prayer, and the pillars of Islam. And we do not declare him a disbeliever for contradicting consensus (ijma); for we have a consideration in declaring an-Nazzam a disbeliever for denying the principle of consensus; because the doubt is great concerning consensus being a decisive proof. Consensus is merely an agreement on a theoretical opinion. What we are dealing with here is agreement on reporting something perceptible, and the agreement of a large number on reporting something perceptible by way of tawatur produces necessary knowledge. But the agreement of the people of binding and loosing on a single theoretical opinion does not produce knowledge except from the side of the Law. Therefore, it is not permissible to use the tawatur of reports from the investigators who ruled on it to prove the temporal origination of the world; rather, there is no tawatur except in perceptibles. The sixth rank: That he does not explicitly deny, nor does he deny a matter known by definitive tawatur from the fundamentals of religion, but he denies something whose correctness is known by mere consensus (ijma mujarrad), so there is no basis for its correctness except consensus. As for tawatur, it does not attest to it. For example, an-Nazzam, when he denied that consensus is a decisive proof in principle, and said: There is no rational decisive proof nor a mutawatir legal proof that cannot be interpreted to indicate the impossibility of error upon the people of consensus. So all the reports and verses that are cited are interpreted according to his claim. In this statement of his, he violates the consensus of the Successors (tabi'un), for we know their consensus that what the Companions agreed upon is a definite truth, whose opposition is impossible. So he denied consensus and violated consensus. This is in a matter of ijtihad, and I have difficulty with it; for the problems are many concerning the fact that consensus is a proof. That almost becomes a preparation for an excuse. But if this door were opened, it would lead to abominable matters. That is, if someone said: It is permissible that a messenger be sent after our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, then hesitation in declaring him a disbeliever would be far-fetched. The basis for the impossibility of that, upon investigation, is necessarily derived from consensus; for reason does not deem it impossible. And what is transmitted about it from his saying, 'There is no prophet after me,' and from His saying, 'and the seal of the prophets,' this speaker would not be unable to interpret it. He would say: 'The seal of the prophets' means the prophets of determination (ulu al-azm). For His saying 'the prophets' is general, and it is not unlikely to specify a general. And his saying 'There is no prophet after me' does not refer to a messenger, and there is a difference between a prophet and a messenger, and the prophet is of a higher rank than the messenger... and other types of delirium. This and its likes cannot be claimed to be impossible from the mere wording; for we, in interpreting the apparent meanings of anthropomorphism, have judged by possibilities more remote than these, and that did not nullify the texts. But the refutation of this speaker is that the ummah understood by consensus, from this and from circumstantial evidence of his states, that he made understood that there is no prophet after him ever, and no messenger ever, and that there is no interpretation nor specification in it. So the denier of this is only a denier of consensus. And at this point, many interrelated and tangled issues branch off, each of which requires investigation.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a classification of different levels of denial and their implications for takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever). Imam Ghazali begins by reasserting that a person who denies matters known by tawatur (mass transmission) should be judged a disbeliever, but with a caveat: such matters are grasped by both commoners and elites. However, if the person is a recent convert and the tawatur has not yet reached him, we give him time. Denying something like a specific battle or the marriage of the Prophet does not entail takfir because it is not a fundamental of religion. But denying the Hajj, prayer, or the pillars of Islam does. Then Ghazali turns to consensus (ijma). He says we do not declare a person a disbeliever merely for rejecting consensus because there is a great deal of doubt about whether consensus provides decisive certainty. He distinguishes between tawatur (which produces necessary knowledge) and ijma (which is a theoretical agreement). The sixth rank is when a person does not deny something known by tawatur but denies something known only by mere consensus (ijma mujarrad), such as an-Nazzam denying that consensus is a decisive proof. Ghazali notes that an-Nazzam violated the consensus of the Successors. Ghazali then says this is a matter of ijtihad and he has difficulty with it because there are many problems with consensus being a proof. However, if we open the door to rejecting consensus, it could lead to abominable claims like the possibility of a prophet after Muhammad. Reason alone does not prohibit it; only consensus does. And the denier would interpret the texts. Ghazali argues that the ummah understood by consensus that there is no prophet after Muhammad, and this understanding is based on the Prophet's words and circumstantial evidence. So the denier is essentially a denier of consensus. The passage ends by noting that this issue branches into many interconnected matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that rejecting consensus on a theological issue automatically makes one a disbeliever.
Correction: Ghazali shows hesitation and warns that while consensus is important, its authority is debated, and takfir should not be applied hastily.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the main refutation against someone who claims a prophet can come after Muhammad?
A) Reason proves it is impossible.
B) The literal wording of the Quran prohibits it.
C) The consensus of the ummah understood that no prophet comes after him.
D) The sayings of the Companions explicitly forbid it.

Key Takeaway
Denying matters proven only by consensus is a delicate issue; Ghazali hesitates to declare takfir but warns of dangerous consequences if consensus is entirely rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself disagreeing with the consensus of the righteous scholars (ijma), do you pause to examine whether your reasoning is truly sound, or do you confidently assume that the entire community could be wrong? What does Ghazali's hesitation teach you about the weight of such a disagreement?
?
Consider a belief you hold that is based solely on the consensus of the ummah—such as the impossibility of a prophet after Muhammad. Have you ever truly felt the weight of that consensus as a divine protection, or do you take it for granted? What would it mean for you if you found yourself tempted to interpret away texts as the hypothetical denier did?
?
Ghazali warns that opening the door to rejecting consensus leads to 'abominable matters.' Is there an area in your life where you have allowed small deviations to grow because you neglected the collective wisdom of the community? How can you strengthen your commitment to the consensus of the Salaf?
